## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration as a function of time and its own concentration. The rate law dA/dt = f(A, t) suggests either a simple nth-order reaction or a more complex mechanism where other species have been expressed in terms of A and t.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (reaction with constant source/sink)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (approach to equilibrium, A_eq absorbed in c1)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturating kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis where product catalyzes reaction)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Fractional order with time: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (diffusion-limited or heterogeneous catalysis)
- Consecutive mechanism reduced: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (elimination of intermediate species)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood surface: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed bimolecular reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Integer power dependence on concentration → classical elementary reaction order (1st, 2nd, 3rd order kinetics)
- Rational function of concentration (A/(c+A)) → saturation or enzyme-mediated mechanism with limited active sites
- Product of concentration and complement (A*(c-A)) → autocatalytic or logistic growth in chemical systems
- Exponential dependence on time → Arrhenius-type temperature ramping or photochemical intensity variation
- Sum of power-law terms in A → parallel competing reaction pathways with different orders
- Negative sign on leading term → net consumption of reactant (standard decay kinetics)
- Squared denominator in rational form → cooperative binding or surface reaction with competitive adsorption
- Linear combination of A and constant → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium concentration
- Fractional exponent on A → complex mechanism or diffusion-controlled heterogeneous reaction
- Time appearing as multiplicative factor with A → sequential mechanism where intermediate was algebraically eliminated

**GT:** `0.7391218893246799*A**2/(0.8913296033617462*A**4 + 1) - 0.3009370469546767*A*exp(-0.06776739623123975*t)`

This has two terms:
1. A rational term: `k1 * A**2 / (k2 * A**4 + 1)` — which can be rewritten as `A**2 / (c*A**4 + d)` form
2. An exponential decay term: `k3 * A * exp(-k4 * t)`

Note that `A**2/(c*A**4 + 1)` can be rewritten by multiplying numerator and denominator by `1/A**2` as `1/(c*A**2 + 1/A**2)`, but more importantly, it equals `A*[A/(c*A**4+1)]` = `A * [1/(cA**3 + 1/A)]`. Let me also note: `A**2/(A**4*c + d) = (A/c') * 1/(A**2 + d') = ...` Actually, let me think about `A/(A**2 + c)` form: `A/(A**2+c)` is NOT equivalent to `A**2/(A**4+d)` because substituting shows different functional forms.
